bebffd69-f30f-4edf-bf58-5655ba5c5599	Military judge removes prosecutor accused of misconduct in Navy SEAL murder trial	By Samuel Chamberlain | Fox News	<p>The military prosecutor of a decorated Navy SEAL accused of murdering a wounded teenage ISIS prisoner in Iraq was booted from the case by a military judge Monday over unsanctioned tracking of the defense team's emails.</p><p>Capt. Aaron Rugh ordered Cmdr. Christopher Czaplak removed from the case after lawyers for Special Operations Chief Edward "Eddie" Gallagher accused prosecutors of attaching tracking software to emails sent to them and a Navy Times journalist in a bid to find the source of leaks to the media. In his ruling, Rugh said it was not in his power to determine prosecutorial misconduct, but there was the possibility of a conflict of interest that required Czaplak to be removed.</p><p>It was not immediately clear how Rugh's decision would affect Gallagher's trial, which is scheduled to begin June 10. The judge has not ruled on whether to dismiss charges of murder and attempted murder against Gallagher.</p><br/><div style="width:500px; word-wrap:break-word; font-size:80%;"><img src="https://a57.foxnews.com/static.foxnews.com/foxnews.com/content/uploads/2019/06/640/320/eddie-gallagher.jpg?ve=1&tl=1" width=500px style="padding-bottom:0.5em;" /><br/>\n      Navy Special Operations Chief Edward Gallagher leaving a military courtroom alongside wife Andrea in San Diego last Thursday.\n      (AP)</div><br/><p>Navy spokesman Brian O'Rourke told The Associated Press that Czaplak would be replaced with another attorney.</p><p>"Chief Petty Officer Gallagher is entitled to a fair trial and the Navy is committed to upholding that principle," O'Rourke said. The defense team has said that even if a new prosecutor is named, Gallagher can't get a fair trial.</p><p>It is extremely unusual for a military judge to remove the prosecution or dismiss a case only days before the start of a trial. Rugh ordered Gallagher released from custody last week after the email tracking came to light.</p><p>At a hearing on the matter Friday, prosecutor Lt. Scott McDonald claimed the tracking effort was to collect data such as IP addresses, which have no expectation of privacy, and was not meant to snoop on the content of the emails.</p><br/><div style="width:500px; word-wrap:break-word; font-size:80%;"><img src="https://a57.foxnews.com/static.foxnews.com/foxnews.com/content/uploads/2019/06/640/320/cmdrczaplak720.jpg?ve=1&tl=1" width=500px style="padding-bottom:0.5em;" /><br/>\n      Cmdr. Christopher Czaplak\n      (U.S. Navy)</div><br/><p>"We're talking about raw data," said McDonald, who argued that "even if there was some intrusion" in violation of attorney-client privilege, it didn't rise to the level necessary to dismiss the case.</p><p>But, Rugh chided Navy investigators who refused to testify Friday about who authorized the tracking scheme, saying the "lack of candor or cooperation in this process, I think, could be huge as a sign of culpability." The defense discovered the tracking code hidden in a suspicious logo of an American flag with a bald eagle perched on the scales of justice beneath Czaplak's signature.</p><p>Rugh indicated Friday he was misled about the tracking effort. He said investigators told him privately they planned to embed code in what he believed to be a court document to help them find the source of leaks but the judge said he didn't have the power to authorize such a tactic and wasn't told they planned to target emails sent to the defense lawyers or a journalist.</p><p>Gallagher is accused of stabbing to death a 15-year old ISIS fighter in Iraq in 2017, shooting two civilians in the same year and opening fire on crowds, all charges to which he has pleaded not guilty.</p><p>His platoon supervisor, Lt. Jacob Portier, has been fighting charges of conduct unbecoming an officer for allegedly conducting Gallagher's re-enlistment ceremony next to the militant's corpse.</p><p>The case has drawn the attention of President Trump, who reportedly has considered pardoning Gallagher along with other U.S. troops accused or convicted of war crimes.</p><p><i>Fox News' Vandana Rambaran and The Associated Press contributed to this report.</i></p>	https://www.foxnews.com/us/navy-seal-eddie-gallagher-prosecutor-removed-military-judge		2019-06-06 06:07:11.041991

Jacob Portier, has been fighting charges of conduct unbecoming an officer for allegedly conducting Gallagher's re-enlistment ceremony next to the militant's corpse.</p><p>The case has drawn the attention of President Trump, who reportedly has considered pardoning Gallagher along with other U.S. troops accused or convicted of war crimes.</p><p><i>Fox News' Vandana Rambaran and The Associated Press contributed to this report.</i></p>	https://www.foxnews.com/us/navy-seal-eddie-gallagher-prosecutor-removed-military-judge		2019-06-06 06:07:18.13895
3ca7f719-5a9d-4284-9760-8d7cd75b04fb	Can't tell Lil Nas X nothin': How 'Old Town Road' changed his life and how he aims to prove his country chops	By ASHAN SINGH, KATIE MULDOWNEY, LAURA COBURN and ALLIE YANG	<p>“Old Town Road” is the hottest song in the world right now.</p><p>It was an instant viral hit that has spent the last eight weeks at No. 1 on Billboard’s Hot 100. It went triple platinum in May and has been streamed over one billion times.</p><p>But the song also gained notoriety for sparking a national debate over whether a rapper, who happens to be black, can create a country hit.</p><p>The hit single, “Old Town Road,” has caused divisions within the music industry.</p><p>But the controversy has united an unlikely pairing between a country legend, Billy Ray Cyrus and a rising star: 20-year-old rapper Lil Nas X.</p><p>And he’s not going away.</p><p>“This is only the beginning. And you know people won't realize that until they realize it,” the artist, born Montero Lamar Hill, told “Nightline.” “I knew for a fact that this song would take me to another level but … I can’t say I knew that it was going to be worldwide or nationwide.”</p><br/><div style="width:500px; word-wrap:break-word; font-size:80%;"><img src="https://s.abcnews.com/images/US/old-town-road-01-gty-jt-190530_hpMain_4x3_992.jpg" width=500px style="padding-bottom:0.5em;" /><br/>Lil Nas X performs on May 9, 2019 in Los Angeles.</div><br/><p>For Hill, all of this seemed unfathomable less than a year ago. A college dropout, Hill was living on his sister’s couch in Atlanta, trying to get anyone to listen to his songs.</p><p>“Life was me moving from sibling to sibling[‘s] house, promoting my music through Twitter… barely getting a reaction out of anything,” he said. “Then I find this beat on YouTube which is ‘Old Town Road,’ beat by this guy named Young Kio… and I made this song.”</p><p>He paid $30 for the beat and released the track independently.</p><p>“I first started with a tweet and it was already having some momentum. And then … over the course of a few months, I would just [put] it into memes and kind of forcing it into the Internet, in a way … it started to catch on,” Hill said.</p><p>The song went viral on the video sharing platform Tik Tok. Before he knew it, Lil Nas X found himself on Billboard’s country chart, debuting at No. 19.</p><p>“If you don't know what Tik Tok is, that just means you're older than 15,” said Joe Levy, a contributing editor at Rolling Stone magazine. “'Old Town Road’ became a meme on Tik Tok. People would drink something called ‘yeehaw juice’ and the song would start up and they might be dancing in a hip-hop manner and they would jump in the air and transform into cowboys.”</p><p>Brittany Hennessy, the author of the book "Influencer" and the cofounder of CARBON said a catchy hook or a “strange” wild line can turn a song into a meme. With “Old Town Road,” she said, “it's that ‘I got horses in the back.’ And for some reason that's what people latched on.”</p><p>Hill said social media helped the song go viral.</p><p>“Social media is the biggest factor in every song is nowadays,” he said. “It's like I use that to my advantage… and it worked.”</p><p>Now it seems like everyone wants in. Celebrities like Kim Kardashian West, Tom Brady and Keith Urban are fans.</p><p>Jem Aswad, senior music editor at Variety, said “Old Town Road” is “one of the biggest songs of the year if not the biggest.”</p><p>But less than a week after the song landed on the Billboard charts, “Old Town Road” got the boot. In a statement to Rolling Stone, Billboard said the track “does not embrace enough elements of today’s country music to chart in its current version.”</p><p>That decision led to outrage online, with some fans crying discrimination.</p><p>“I can't control what people would think. You know people always want to say something,” Hill said. “But … I know what it is.”</p><p>The controversy caught the attention of country legend Billy Ray Cyrus.</p><p>“I just thought, ‘Wait, that's not fair,’” Cyrus told “Nightline.” “Waylon [Jennings] being one of the greatest outlaws in the history of country music, and he said to me ‘the definition of an outlaw is one who has been outlawed.’”</p><p>Cyrus said he thought the song “was a smash.”</p><p>“When I hear something, I don't necessarily try to define it by what is its musical genre,” he continued. “I say ‘do I relate to that song? Does it feel like my roots?' 'Old Town Road’ was all of me-- it was my past, present and future. It had everything that I'd been raised on my whole life -- banjo, bluegrass and [a] solid country hook.”</p><p>Hill said Cyrus is a “cultural icon” and that his collaboration took the song “to a new level. Definitely.”</p><br/><div style="width:500px; word-wrap:break-word; font-size:80%;"><img src="https://s.abcnews.com/images/US/old-town-road-03-gty-jt-190530_hpEmbed_16x11_992.jpg" width=500px style="padding-bottom:0.5em;" /><br/>Billy Ray Cyrus (L) and Lil Nas X pose backstage during the 2019 Stagecoach Festival on April 28, 2019 in Indio, Calif. </div><br/><p>"Country music is a song that touches people's heart, especially country music fans. If country music fans dig it, then it's country," Cyrus explained.</p><p>And country fans do love it. The unlikely duo teamed up for a remix of “Old Town Road” for an epic, star-studded music video.</p><p>Cyrus said the beauty of the song’s success is “the fans."</p><p>“It was about people driving the song, not about a critic saying ‘no, this doesn’t fit our rulebook,’” he said.</p><br/><div style="width:500px; word-wrap:break-word; font-size:80%;"><img src="https://s.abcnews.com/images/US/old-town-road-02-gty-jt-190530_hpEmbed_3x2_992.jpg" width=500px style="padding-bottom:0.5em;" /><br/>Billy Ray Cyrus and Lil Nas X perform on April 28, 2019 in Indio, Calif.</div><br/><p>“I'm 57 years old and never thought I'd feel anything like this ever again,” Cyrus went on. “I've been a part of a couple of things that were described at the time as a phenomenon, including ‘Achy Breaky Heart’ and Hannah Montana. And this song, and this moment, and this movement feels like all of that plus more.”</p><p>Cyrus said Hill “doesn’t need any advice” from him, adding, “Think like there is no box. In today's world you don't have to limit yourself to one particular style or genre. Be it all.”</p><p>Aswad pointed out that country music has gone through a transformation over the past decade.</p><p>“A lot of what's popular in country right now a lot of people 10 years ago would not have considered to be country songs,” he said. “Country has become very rock and roll in a lot of ways. And there's all this pop crossover … so all bets are off.</p><p>But not everyone agrees. Last week, after announcing his collaboration with Wrangler, Hill faced more backlash, furthering the debate on what it means to be “country.”</p><p>Wrangler tweeted a response to one customer, saying: “As an iconic brand in fashion, we have shown up in music, film and popular culture for decades. Our Western heritage and offering a quality and versatile product for all wearers will always be the very heart of our brand.”</p><p>The haters haven’t stopped Hill. Since then, he’s been everywhere. Just this week, Hill surprised a group of elementary school children in Ohio, performed in Boston ahead of Game 1 of the Stanley Cup series and scored the new “Rambo” trailer. “Nightline” was with him and Cyrus when Hill took the stage for the first time ever at the Stagecoach Festival in April.</p><p>“Lil Nas X Definitely has special sauce because he decided he wanted it to go viral and he did it,” Hennessy said. “It's not just about making something that you think people will like. It's actually making something that people can like and then making their own because that's what makes them share.”</p><p>This month, Hill will be releasing an EP and an album will likely follow.</p><p>“I just know they're both going do great and people going to love it,” he said.</p>	https://abcnews.go.com/Entertainment/lil-nas-nothin-town-road-changed-life-aims/story?id=63382846		2019-06-06 06:07:26.482416

You know people always want to say something,” Hill said. “But … I know what it is.”</p><p>The controversy caught the attention of country legend Billy Ray Cyrus.</p><p>“I just thought, ‘Wait, that's not fair,’” Cyrus told “Nightline.” “Waylon [Jennings] being one of the greatest outlaws in the history of country music, and he said to me ‘the definition of an outlaw is one who has been outlawed.’”</p><p>Cyrus said he thought the song “was a smash.”</p><p>“When I hear something, I don't necessarily try to define it by what is its musical genre,” he continued. “I say ‘do I relate to that song? Does it feel like my roots?' 'Old Town Road’ was all of me-- it was my past, present and future. It had everything that I'd been raised on my whole life -- banjo, bluegrass and [a] solid country hook.”</p><p>Hill said Cyrus is a “cultural icon” and that his collaboration took the song “to a new level. Definitely.”</p><br/><div style="width:500px; word-wrap:break-word; font-size:80%;"><img src="https://s.abcnews.com/images/US/old-town-road-03-gty-jt-190530_hpEmbed_16x11_992.jpg" width=500px style="padding-bottom:0.5em;" /><br/>Billy Ray Cyrus (L) and Lil Nas X pose backstage during the 2019 Stagecoach Festival on April 28, 2019 in Indio, Calif. </div><br/><p>"Country music is a song that touches people's heart, especially country music fans. If country music fans dig it, then it's country," Cyrus explained.</p><p>And country fans do love it. The unlikely duo teamed up for a remix of “Old Town Road” for an epic, star-studded music video.</p><p>Cyrus said the beauty of the song’s success is “the fans."</p><p>“It was about people driving the song, not about a critic saying ‘no, this doesn’t fit our rulebook,’” he said.</p><br/><div style="width:500px; word-wrap:break-word; font-size:80%;"><img src="https://s.abcnews.com/images/US/old-town-road-02-gty-jt-190530_hpEmbed_3x2_992.jpg" width=500px style="padding-bottom:0.5em;" /><br/>Billy Ray Cyrus and Lil Nas X perform on April 28, 2019 in Indio, Calif.</div><br/><p>“I'm 57 years old and never thought I'd feel anything like this ever again,” Cyrus went on. “I've been a part of a couple of things that were described at the time as a phenomenon, including ‘Achy Breaky Heart’ and Hannah Montana. And this song, and this moment, and this movement feels like all of that plus more.”</p><p>Cyrus said Hill “doesn’t need any advice” from him, adding, “Think like there is no box. In today's world you don't have to limit yourself to one particular style or genre. Be it all.”</p><p>Aswad pointed out that country music has gone through a transformation over the past decade.</p><p>“A lot of what's popular in country right now a lot of people 10 years ago would not have considered to be country songs,” he said. “Country has become very rock and roll in a lot of ways. And there's all this pop crossover … so all bets are off.</p><p>But not everyone agrees. Last week, after announcing his collaboration with Wrangler, Hill faced more backlash, furthering the debate on what it means to be “country.”</p><p>Wrangler tweeted a response to one customer, saying: “As an iconic brand in fashion, we have shown up in music, film and popular culture for decades. Our Western heritage and offering a quality and versatile product for all wearers will always be the very heart of our brand.”</p><p>The haters haven’t stopped Hill. Since then, he’s been everywhere. Just this week, Hill surprised a group of elementary school children in Ohio, performed in Boston ahead of Game 1 of the Stanley Cup series and scored the new “Rambo” trailer. “Nightline” was with him and Cyrus when Hill took the stage for the first time ever at the Stagecoach Festival in April.</p><p>“Lil Nas X Definitely has special sauce because he decided he wanted it to go viral and he did it,” Hennessy said. “It's not just about making something that you think people will like. It's actually making something that people can like and then making their own because that's what makes them share.”</p><p>This month, Hill will be releasing an EP and an album will likely follow.</p><p>“I just know they're both going do great and people going to love it,” he said.</p>	https://abcnews.go.com/Entertainment/lil-nas-nothin-town-road-changed-life-aims/story?id=63382846	changchaishi	2019-06-06 05:46:18.697355

fc167e74-c8b6-4afe-bc09-b8fcd2bc4fb1	Can't tell Lil Nas X nothin': How 'Old Town Road' changed his life and how he aims to prove his country chops	By ASHAN SINGH, KATIE MULDOWNEY, LAURA COBURN and ALLIE YANG	<p>“Old Town Road” is the hottest song in the world right now.</p><p>It was an instant viral hit that has spent the last eight weeks at No. 1 on Billboard’s Hot 100. It went triple platinum in May and has been streamed over one billion times.</p><p>But the song also gained notoriety for sparking a national debate over whether a rapper, who happens to be black, can create a country hit.</p><p>The hit single, “Old Town Road,” has caused divisions within the music industry.</p><p>But the controversy has united an unlikely pairing between a country legend, Billy Ray Cyrus and a rising star: 20-year-old rapper Lil Nas X.</p><p>And he’s not going away.</p><p>“This is only the beginning. And you know people won't realize that until they realize it,” the artist, born Montero Lamar Hill, told “Nightline.” “I knew for a fact that this song would take me to another level but … I can’t say I knew that it was going to be worldwide or nationwide.”</p><br/><div style="width:500px; word-wrap:break-word; font-size:80%;"><img src="https://s.abcnews.com/images/US/old-town-road-01-gty-jt-190530_hpMain_4x3_992.jpg" width=500px style="padding-bottom:0.5em;" /><br/>Lil Nas X performs on May 9, 2019 in Los Angeles.</div><br/><p>For Hill, all of this seemed unfathomable less than a year ago. A college dropout, Hill was living on his sister’s couch in Atlanta, trying to get anyone to listen to his songs.</p><p>“Life was me moving from sibling to sibling[‘s] house, promoting my music through Twitter… barely getting a reaction out of anything,” he said. “Then I find this beat on YouTube which is ‘Old Town Road,’ beat by this guy named Young Kio… and I made this song.”</p><p>He paid $30 for the beat and released the track independently.</p><p>“I first started with a tweet and it was already having some momentum. And then … over the course of a few months, I would just [put] it into memes and kind of forcing it into the Internet, in a way … it started to catch on,” Hill said.</p><p>The song went viral on the video sharing platform Tik Tok. Before he knew it, Lil Nas X found himself on Billboard’s country chart, debuting at No. 19.</p><p>“If you don't know what Tik Tok is, that just means you're older than 15,” said Joe Levy, a contributing editor at Rolling Stone magazine. “'Old Town Road’ became a meme on Tik Tok. People would drink something called ‘yeehaw juice’ and the song would start up and they might be dancing in a hip-hop manner and they would jump in the air and transform into cowboys.”</p><p>Brittany Hennessy, the author of the book "Influencer" and the cofounder of CARBON said a catchy hook or a “strange” wild line can turn a song into a meme. With “Old Town Road,” she said, “it's that ‘I got horses in the back.’ And for some reason that's what people latched on.”</p><p>Hill said social media helped the song go viral.</p><p>“Social media is the biggest factor in every song is nowadays,” he said. “It's like I use that to my advantage… and it worked.”</p><p>Now it seems like everyone wants in. Celebrities like Kim Kardashian West, Tom Brady and Keith Urban are fans.</p><p>Jem Aswad, senior music editor at Variety, said “Old Town Road” is “one of the biggest songs of the year if not the biggest.”</p><p>But less than a week after the song landed on the Billboard charts, “Old Town Road” got the boot. In a statement to Rolling Stone, Billboard said the track “does not embrace enough elements of today’s country music to chart in its current version.”</p><p>That decision led to outrage online, with some fans crying discrimination.</p><p>“I can't control what people would think. You know people always want to say something,” Hill said. “But … I know what it is.”</p><p>The controversy caught the attention of country legend Billy Ray Cyrus.</p><p>“I just thought, ‘Wait, that's not fair,’” Cyrus told “Nightline.” “Waylon [Jennings] being one of the greatest outlaws in the history of country music, and he said to me ‘the definition of an outlaw is one who has been outlawed.’”</p><p>Cyrus said he thought the song “was a smash.”</p><p>“When I hear something, I don't necessarily try to define it by what is its musical genre,” he continued. “I say ‘do I relate to that song? Does it feel like my roots?' 'Old Town Road’ was all of me-- it was my past, present and future. It had everything that I'd been raised on my whole life -- banjo, bluegrass and [a] solid country hook.”</p><p>Hill said Cyrus is a “cultural icon” and that his collaboration took the song “to a new level. Definitely.”</p><br/><div style="width:500px; word-wrap:break-word; font-size:80%;"><img src="https://s.abcnews.com/images/US/old-town-road-03-gty-jt-190530_hpEmbed_16x11_992.jpg" width=500px style="padding-bottom:0.5em;" /><br/>Billy Ray Cyrus (L) and Lil Nas X pose backstage during the 2019 Stagecoach Festival on April 28, 2019 in Indio, Calif. </div><br/><p>"Country music is a song that touches people's heart, especially country music fans. If country music fans dig it, then it's country," Cyrus explained.</p><p>And country fans do love it. The unlikely duo teamed up for a remix of “Old Town Road” for an epic, star-studded music video.</p><p>Cyrus said the beauty of the song’s success is “the fans."</p><p>“It was about people driving the song, not about a critic saying ‘no, this doesn’t fit our rulebook,’” he said.</p><br/><div style="width:500px; word-wrap:break-word; font-size:80%;"><img src="https://s.abcnews.com/images/US/old-town-road-02-gty-jt-190530_hpEmbed_3x2_992.jpg" width=500px style="padding-bottom:0.5em;" /><br/>Billy Ray Cyrus and Lil Nas X perform on April 28, 2019 in Indio, Calif.</div><br/><p>“I'm 57 years old and never thought I'd feel anything like this ever again,” Cyrus went on. “I've been a part of a couple of things that were described at the time as a phenomenon, including ‘Achy Breaky Heart’ and Hannah Montana. And this song, and this moment, and this movement feels like all of that plus more.”</p><p>Cyrus said Hill “doesn’t need any advice” from him, adding, “Think like there is no box. In today's world you don't have to limit yourself to one particular style or genre. Be it all.”</p><p>Aswad pointed out that country music has gone through a transformation over the past decade.</p><p>“A lot of what's popular in country right now a lot of people 10 years ago would not have considered to be country songs,” he said. “Country has become very rock and roll in a lot of ways. And there's all this pop crossover … so all bets are off.</p><p>But not everyone agrees. Last week, after announcing his collaboration with Wrangler, Hill faced more backlash, furthering the debate on what it means to be “country.”</p><p>Wrangler tweeted a response to one customer, saying: “As an iconic brand in fashion, we have shown up in music, film and popular culture for decades. Our Western heritage and offering a quality and versatile product for all wearers will always be the very heart of our brand.”</p><p>The haters haven’t stopped Hill. Since then, he’s been everywhere. Just this week, Hill surprised a group of elementary school children in Ohio, performed in Boston ahead of Game 1 of the Stanley Cup series and scored the new “Rambo” trailer. “Nightline” was with him and Cyrus when Hill took the stage for the first time ever at the Stagecoach Festival in April.</p><p>“Lil Nas X Definitely has special sauce because he decided he wanted it to go viral and he did it,” Hennessy said. “It's not just about making something that you think people will like. It's actually making something that people can like and then making their own because that's what makes them share.”</p><p>This month, Hill will be releasing an EP and an album will likely follow.</p><p>“I just know they're both going do great and people going to love it,” he said.</p>	https://abcnews.go.com/Entertainment/lil-nas-nothin-town-road-changed-life-aims/story?id=63382846		2019-06-06 07:06:19.386627

cafbac8a-9e1c-4ae4-a4a9-fad56d8b36d2	Military judge removes prosecutor accused of misconduct in Navy SEAL murder trial	By Samuel Chamberlain | Fox News	<p>The military prosecutor of a decorated Navy SEAL accused of murdering a wounded teenage ISIS prisoner in Iraq was booted from the case by a military judge Monday over unsanctioned tracking of the defense team's emails.</p><p>Capt. Aaron Rugh ordered Cmdr. Christopher Czaplak removed from the case after lawyers for Special Operations Chief Edward "Eddie" Gallagher accused prosecutors of attaching tracking software to emails sent to them and a Navy Times journalist in a bid to find the source of leaks to the media. In his ruling, Rugh said it was not in his power to determine prosecutorial misconduct, but there was the possibility of a conflict of interest that required Czaplak to be removed.</p><p>It was not immediately clear how Rugh's decision would affect Gallagher's trial, which is scheduled to begin June 10. The judge has not ruled on whether to dismiss charges of murder and attempted murder against Gallagher.</p><br/><div style="width:500px; word-wrap:break-word; font-size:80%;"><img src="https://a57.foxnews.com/static.foxnews.com/foxnews.com/content/uploads/2019/06/640/320/eddie-gallagher.jpg?ve=1&tl=1" width=500px style="padding-bottom:0.5em;" /><br/>\n      Navy Special Operations Chief Edward Gallagher leaving a military courtroom alongside wife Andrea in San Diego last Thursday.\n      (AP)</div><br/><p>Navy spokesman Brian O'Rourke told The Associated Press that Czaplak would be replaced with another attorney.</p><p>"Chief Petty Officer Gallagher is entitled to a fair trial and the Navy is committed to upholding that principle," O'Rourke said. The defense team has said that even if a new prosecutor is named, Gallagher can't get a fair trial.</p><p>It is extremely unusual for a military judge to remove the prosecution or dismiss a case only days before the start of a trial. Rugh ordered Gallagher released from custody last week after the email tracking came to light.</p><p>At a hearing on the matter Friday, prosecutor Lt. Scott McDonald claimed the tracking effort was to collect data such as IP addresses, which have no expectation of privacy, and was not meant to snoop on the content of the emails.</p><br/><div style="width:500px; word-wrap:break-word; font-size:80%;"><img src="https://a57.foxnews.com/static.foxnews.com/foxnews.com/content/uploads/2019/06/640/320/cmdrczaplak720.jpg?ve=1&tl=1" width=500px style="padding-bottom:0.5em;" /><br/>\n      Cmdr. Christopher Czaplak\n      (U.S. Navy)</div><br/><p>"We're talking about raw data," said McDonald, who argued that "even if there was some intrusion" in violation of attorney-client privilege, it didn't rise to the level necessary to dismiss the case.</p><p>But, Rugh chided Navy investigators who refused to testify Friday about who authorized the tracking scheme, saying the "lack of candor or cooperation in this process, I think, could be huge as a sign of culpability." The defense discovered the tracking code hidden in a suspicious logo of an American flag with a bald eagle perched on the scales of justice beneath Czaplak's signature.</p><p>Rugh indicated Friday he was misled about the tracking effort. He said investigators told him privately they planned to embed code in what he believed to be a court document to help them find the source of leaks but the judge said he didn't have the power to authorize such a tactic and wasn't told they planned to target emails sent to the defense lawyers or a journalist.</p><p>Gallagher is accused of stabbing to death a 15-year old ISIS fighter in Iraq in 2017, shooting two civilians in the same year and opening fire on crowds, all charges to which he has pleaded not guilty.</p><p>His platoon supervisor, Lt. Jacob Portier, has been fighting charges of conduct unbecoming an officer for allegedly conducting Gallagher's re-enlistment ceremony next to the militant's corpse.</p><p>The case has drawn the attention of President Trump, who reportedly has considered pardoning Gallagher along with other U.S. troops accused or convicted of war crimes.</p><p><i>Fox News' Vandana Rambaran and The Associated Press contributed to this report.</i></p>	https://www.foxnews.com/us/navy-seal-eddie-gallagher-prosecutor-removed-military-judge		2019-06-06 07:26:56.703447

5be034db-63ce-44e5-9f23-6be4e73b5650	Military judge removes prosecutor accused of misconduct in Navy SEAL murder trial	By Samuel Chamberlain | Fox News	<p>The military prosecutor of a decorated Navy SEAL accused of murdering a wounded teenage ISIS prisoner in Iraq was booted from the case by a military judge Monday over unsanctioned tracking of the defense team's emails.</p><p>Capt. Aaron Rugh ordered Cmdr. Christopher Czaplak removed from the case after lawyers for Special Operations Chief Edward "Eddie" Gallagher accused prosecutors of attaching tracking software to emails sent to them and a Navy Times journalist in a bid to find the source of leaks to the media. In his ruling, Rugh said it was not in his power to determine prosecutorial misconduct, but there was the possibility of a conflict of interest that required Czaplak to be removed.</p><p>It was not immediately clear how Rugh's decision would affect Gallagher's trial, which is scheduled to begin June 10. The judge has not ruled on whether to dismiss charges of murder and attempted murder against Gallagher.</p><br/><div style="width:500px; word-wrap:break-word; font-size:80%;"><img src="https://a57.foxnews.com/static.foxnews.com/foxnews.com/content/uploads/2019/06/640/320/eddie-gallagher.jpg?ve=1&tl=1" width=500px style="padding-bottom:0.5em;" /><br/>\n      Navy Special Operations Chief Edward Gallagher leaving a military courtroom alongside wife Andrea in San Diego last Thursday.\n      (AP)</div><br/><p>Navy spokesman Brian O'Rourke told The Associated Press that Czaplak would be replaced with another attorney.</p><p>"Chief Petty Officer Gallagher is entitled to a fair trial and the Navy is committed to upholding that principle," O'Rourke said. The defense team has said that even if a new prosecutor is named, Gallagher can't get a fair trial.</p><p>It is extremely unusual for a military judge to remove the prosecution or dismiss a case only days before the start of a trial. Rugh ordered Gallagher released from custody last week after the email tracking came to light.</p><p>At a hearing on the matter Friday, prosecutor Lt. Scott McDonald claimed the tracking effort was to collect data such as IP addresses, which have no expectation of privacy, and was not meant to snoop on the content of the emails.</p><br/><div style="width:500px; word-wrap:break-word; font-size:80%;"><img src="https://a57.foxnews.com/static.foxnews.com/foxnews.com/content/uploads/2019/06/640/320/cmdrczaplak720.jpg?ve=1&tl=1" width=500px style="padding-bottom:0.5em;" /><br/>\n      Cmdr. Christopher Czaplak\n      (U.S. Navy)</div><br/><p>"We're talking about raw data," said McDonald, who argued that "even if there was some intrusion" in violation of attorney-client privilege, it didn't rise to the level necessary to dismiss the case.</p><p>But, Rugh chided Navy investigators who refused to testify Friday about who authorized the tracking scheme, saying the "lack of candor or cooperation in this process, I think, could be huge as a sign of culpability." The defense discovered the tracking code hidden in a suspicious logo of an American flag with a bald eagle perched on the scales of justice beneath Czaplak's signature.</p><p>Rugh indicated Friday he was misled about the tracking effort. He said investigators told him privately they planned to embed code in what he believed to be a court document to help them find the source of leaks but the judge said he didn't have the power to authorize such a tactic and wasn't told they planned to target emails sent to the defense lawyers or a journalist.</p><p>Gallagher is accused of stabbing to death a 15-year old ISIS fighter in Iraq in 2017, shooting two civilians in the same year and opening fire on crowds, all charges to which he has pleaded not guilty.</p><p>His platoon supervisor, Lt. Jacob Portier, has been fighting charges of conduct unbecoming an officer for allegedly conducting Gallagher's re-enlistment ceremony next to the militant's corpse.</p><p>The case has drawn the attention of President Trump, who reportedly has considered pardoning Gallagher along with other U.S. troops accused or convicted of war crimes.</p><p><i>Fox News' Vandana Rambaran and The Associated Press contributed to this report.</i></p>	https://www.foxnews.com/us/navy-seal-eddie-gallagher-prosecutor-removed-military-judge	111	2019-06-06 07:26:59.769564

ff4f1867-c2e0-433c-8384-7dad11b2185f	Military judge removes prosecutor accused of misconduct in Navy SEAL murder trial	By Samuel Chamberlain | Fox News	<p>The military prosecutor of a decorated Navy SEAL accused of murdering a wounded teenage ISIS prisoner in Iraq was booted from the case by a military judge Monday over unsanctioned tracking of the defense team's emails.</p><p>Capt. Aaron Rugh ordered Cmdr. Christopher Czaplak removed from the case after lawyers for Special Operations Chief Edward "Eddie" Gallagher accused prosecutors of attaching tracking software to emails sent to them and a Navy Times journalist in a bid to find the source of leaks to the media. In his ruling, Rugh said it was not in his power to determine prosecutorial misconduct, but there was the possibility of a conflict of interest that required Czaplak to be removed.</p><p>It was not immediately clear how Rugh's decision would affect Gallagher's trial, which is scheduled to begin June 10. The judge has not ruled on whether to dismiss charges of murder and attempted murder against Gallagher.</p><br/><div style="width:500px; word-wrap:break-word; font-size:80%;"><img src="https://a57.foxnews.com/static.foxnews.com/foxnews.com/content/uploads/2019/06/640/320/eddie-gallagher.jpg?ve=1&tl=1" width=500px style="padding-bottom:0.5em;" /><br/>\n      Navy Special Operations Chief Edward Gallagher leaving a military courtroom alongside wife Andrea in San Diego last Thursday.\n      (AP)</div><br/><p>Navy spokesman Brian O'Rourke told The Associated Press that Czaplak would be replaced with another attorney.</p><p>"Chief Petty Officer Gallagher is entitled to a fair trial and the Navy is committed to upholding that principle," O'Rourke said. The defense team has said that even if a new prosecutor is named, Gallagher can't get a fair trial.</p><p>It is extremely unusual for a military judge to remove the prosecution or dismiss a case only days before the start of a trial. Rugh ordered Gallagher released from custody last week after the email tracking came to light.</p><p>At a hearing on the matter Friday, prosecutor Lt. Scott McDonald claimed the tracking effort was to collect data such as IP addresses, which have no expectation of privacy, and was not meant to snoop on the content of the emails.</p><br/><div style="width:500px; word-wrap:break-word; font-size:80%;"><img src="https://a57.foxnews.com/static.foxnews.com/foxnews.com/content/uploads/2019/06/640/320/cmdrczaplak720.jpg?ve=1&tl=1" width=500px style="padding-bottom:0.5em;" /><br/>\n      Cmdr. Christopher Czaplak\n      (U.S. Navy)</div><br/><p>"We're talking about raw data," said McDonald, who argued that "even if there was some intrusion" in violation of attorney-client privilege, it didn't rise to the level necessary to dismiss the case.</p><p>But, Rugh chided Navy investigators who refused to testify Friday about who authorized the tracking scheme, saying the "lack of candor or cooperation in this process, I think, could be huge as a sign of culpability." The defense discovered the tracking code hidden in a suspicious logo of an American flag with a bald eagle perched on the scales of justice beneath Czaplak's signature.</p><p>Rugh indicated Friday he was misled about the tracking effort. He said investigators told him privately they planned to embed code in what he believed to be a court document to help them find the source of leaks but the judge said he didn't have the power to authorize such a tactic and wasn't told they planned to target emails sent to the defense lawyers or a journalist.</p><p>Gallagher is accused of stabbing to death a 15-year old ISIS fighter in Iraq in 2017, shooting two civilians in the same year and opening fire on crowds, all charges to which he has pleaded not guilty.</p><p>His platoon supervisor, Lt. Jacob Portier, has been fighting charges of conduct unbecoming an officer for allegedly conducting Gallagher's re-enlistment ceremony next to the militant's corpse.</p><p>The case has drawn the attention of President Trump, who reportedly has considered pardoning Gallagher along with other U.S. troops accused or convicted of war crimes.</p><p><i>Fox News' Vandana Rambaran and The Associated Press contributed to this report.</i></p>	https://www.foxnews.com/us/navy-seal-eddie-gallagher-prosecutor-removed-military-judge		2019-06-06 05:58:36.834601
f8060063-77ca-4d19-8b08-a078fdfc8b04	Can't tell Lil Nas X nothin': How 'Old Town Road' changed his life and how he aims to prove his country chops	By ASHAN SINGH, KATIE MULDOWNEY, LAURA COBURN and ALLIE YANG	<p>“Old Town Road” is the hottest song in the world right now.</p><p>It was an instant viral hit that has spent the last eight weeks at No. 1 on Billboard’s Hot 100. It went triple platinum in May and has been streamed over one billion times.</p><p>But the song also gained notoriety for sparking a national debate over whether a rapper, who happens to be black, can create a country hit.</p><p>The hit single, “Old Town Road,” has caused divisions within the music industry.</p><p>But the controversy has united an unlikely pairing between a country legend, Billy Ray Cyrus and a rising star: 20-year-old rapper Lil Nas X.</p><p>And he’s not going away.</p><p>“This is only the beginning. And you know people won't realize that until they realize it,” the artist, born Montero Lamar Hill, told “Nightline.” “I knew for a fact that this song would take me to another level but … I can’t say I knew that it was going to be worldwide or nationwide.”</p><br/><div style="width:500px; word-wrap:break-word; font-size:80%;"><img src="https://s.abcnews.com/images/US/old-town-road-01-gty-jt-190530_hpMain_4x3_992.jpg" width=500px style="padding-bottom:0.5em;" /><br/>Lil Nas X performs on May 9, 2019 in Los Angeles.</div><br/><p>For Hill, all of this seemed unfathomable less than a year ago. A college dropout, Hill was living on his sister’s couch in Atlanta, trying to get anyone to listen to his songs.</p><p>“Life was me moving from sibling to sibling[‘s] house, promoting my music through Twitter… barely getting a reaction out of anything,” he said. “Then I find this beat on YouTube which is ‘Old Town Road,’ beat by this guy named Young Kio… and I made this song.”</p><p>He paid $30 for the beat and released the track independently.</p><p>“I first started with a tweet and it was already having some momentum. And then … over the course of a few months, I would just [put] it into memes and kind of forcing it into the Internet, in a way … it started to catch on,” Hill said.</p><p>The song went viral on the video sharing platform Tik Tok. Before he knew it, Lil Nas X found himself on Billboard’s country chart, debuting at No. 19.</p><p>“If you don't know what Tik Tok is, that just means you're older than 15,” said Joe Levy, a contributing editor at Rolling Stone magazine. “'Old Town Road’ became a meme on Tik Tok. People would drink something called ‘yeehaw juice’ and the song would start up and they might be dancing in a hip-hop manner and they would jump in the air and transform into cowboys.”</p><p>Brittany Hennessy, the author of the book "Influencer" and the cofounder of CARBON said a catchy hook or a “strange” wild line can turn a song into a meme. With “Old Town Road,” she said, “it's that ‘I got horses in the back.’ And for some reason that's what people latched on.”</p><p>Hill said social media helped the song go viral.</p><p>“Social media is the biggest factor in every song is nowadays,” he said. “It's like I use that to my advantage… and it worked.”</p><p>Now it seems like everyone wants in. Celebrities like Kim Kardashian West, Tom Brady and Keith Urban are fans.</p><p>Jem Aswad, senior music editor at Variety, said “Old Town Road” is “one of the biggest songs of the year if not the biggest.”</p><p>But less than a week after the song landed on the Billboard charts, “Old Town Road” got the boot. In a statement to Rolling Stone, Billboard said the track “does not embrace enough elements of today’s country music to chart in its current version.”</p><p>That decision led to outrage online, with some fans crying discrimination.</p><p>“I can't control what people would think. You know people always want to say something,” Hill said. “But … I know what it is.”</p><p>The controversy caught the attention of country legend Billy Ray Cyrus.</p><p>“I just thought, ‘Wait, that's not fair,’” Cyrus told “Nightline.” “Waylon [Jennings] being one of the greatest outlaws in the history of country music, and he said to me ‘the definition of an outlaw is one who has been outlawed.’”</p><p>Cyrus said he thought the song “was a smash.”</p><p>“When I hear something, I don't necessarily try to define it by what is its musical genre,” he continued. “I say ‘do I relate to that song? Does it feel like my roots?' 'Old Town Road’ was all of me-- it was my past, present and future. It had everything that I'd been raised on my whole life -- banjo, bluegrass and [a] solid country hook.”</p><p>Hill said Cyrus is a “cultural icon” and that his collaboration took the song “to a new level. Definitely.”</p><br/><div style="width:500px; word-wrap:break-word; font-size:80%;"><img src="https://s.abcnews.com/images/US/old-town-road-03-gty-jt-190530_hpEmbed_16x11_992.jpg" width=500px style="padding-bottom:0.5em;" /><br/>Billy Ray Cyrus (L) and Lil Nas X pose backstage during the 2019 Stagecoach Festival on April 28, 2019 in Indio, Calif. </div><br/><p>"Country music is a song that touches people's heart, especially country music fans. If country music fans dig it, then it's country," Cyrus explained.</p><p>And country fans do love it. The unlikely duo teamed up for a remix of “Old Town Road” for an epic, star-studded music video.</p><p>Cyrus said the beauty of the song’s success is “the fans."</p><p>“It was about people driving the song, not about a critic saying ‘no, this doesn’t fit our rulebook,’” he said.</p><br/><div style="width:500px; word-wrap:break-word; font-size:80%;"><img src="https://s.abcnews.com/images/US/old-town-road-02-gty-jt-190530_hpEmbed_3x2_992.jpg" width=500px style="padding-bottom:0.5em;" /><br/>Billy Ray Cyrus and Lil Nas X perform on April 28, 2019 in Indio, Calif.</div><br/><p>“I'm 57 years old and never thought I'd feel anything like this ever again,” Cyrus went on. “I've been a part of a couple of things that were described at the time as a phenomenon, including ‘Achy Breaky Heart’ and Hannah Montana. And this song, and this moment, and this movement feels like all of that plus more.”</p><p>Cyrus said Hill “doesn’t need any advice” from him, adding, “Think like there is no box. In today's world you don't have to limit yourself to one particular style or genre. Be it all.”</p><p>Aswad pointed out that country music has gone through a transformation over the past decade.</p><p>“A lot of what's popular in country right now a lot of people 10 years ago would not have considered to be country songs,” he said. “Country has become very rock and roll in a lot of ways. And there's all this pop crossover … so all bets are off.</p><p>But not everyone agrees. Last week, after announcing his collaboration with Wrangler, Hill faced more backlash, furthering the debate on what it means to be “country.”</p><p>Wrangler tweeted a response to one customer, saying: “As an iconic brand in fashion, we have shown up in music, film and popular culture for decades. Our Western heritage and offering a quality and versatile product for all wearers will always be the very heart of our brand.”</p><p>The haters haven’t stopped Hill. Since then, he’s been everywhere. Just this week, Hill surprised a group of elementary school children in Ohio, performed in Boston ahead of Game 1 of the Stanley Cup series and scored the new “Rambo” trailer. “Nightline” was with him and Cyrus when Hill took the stage for the first time ever at the Stagecoach Festival in April.</p><p>“Lil Nas X Definitely has special sauce because he decided he wanted it to go viral and he did it,” Hennessy said. “It's not just about making something that you think people will like. It's actually making something that people can like and then making their own because that's what makes them share.”</p><p>This month, Hill will be releasing an EP and an album will likely follow.</p><p>“I just know they're both going do great and people going to love it,” he said.</p>	https://abcnews.go.com/Entertainment/lil-nas-nothin-town-road-changed-life-aims/story?id=63382846		2019-06-06 05:59:06.378437

4b4574d1-1510-42db-8e0f-cb79224035ba	Military judge removes prosecutor accused of misconduct in Navy SEAL murder trial	By Samuel Chamberlain | Fox News	<p>The military prosecutor of a decorated Navy SEAL accused of murdering a wounded teenage ISIS prisoner in Iraq was booted from the case by a military judge Monday over unsanctioned tracking of the defense team's emails.</p><p>Capt. Aaron Rugh ordered Cmdr. Christopher Czaplak removed from the case after lawyers for Special Operations Chief Edward "Eddie" Gallagher accused prosecutors of attaching tracking software to emails sent to them and a Navy Times journalist in a bid to find the source of leaks to the media. In his ruling, Rugh said it was not in his power to determine prosecutorial misconduct, but there was the possibility of a conflict of interest that required Czaplak to be removed.</p><p>It was not immediately clear how Rugh's decision would affect Gallagher's trial, which is scheduled to begin June 10. The judge has not ruled on whether to dismiss charges of murder and attempted murder against Gallagher.</p><br/><div style="width:500px; word-wrap:break-word; font-size:80%;"><img src="https://a57.foxnews.com/static.foxnews.com/foxnews.com/content/uploads/2019/06/640/320/eddie-gallagher.jpg?ve=1&tl=1" width=500px style="padding-bottom:0.5em;" /><br/>\n      Navy Special Operations Chief Edward Gallagher leaving a military courtroom alongside wife Andrea in San Diego last Thursday.\n      (AP)</div><br/><p>Navy spokesman Brian O'Rourke told The Associated Press that Czaplak would be replaced with another attorney.</p><p>"Chief Petty Officer Gallagher is entitled to a fair trial and the Navy is committed to upholding that principle," O'Rourke said. The defense team has said that even if a new prosecutor is named, Gallagher can't get a fair trial.</p><p>It is extremely unusual for a military judge to remove the prosecution or dismiss a case only days before the start of a trial. Rugh ordered Gallagher released from custody last week after the email tracking came to light.</p><p>At a hearing on the matter Friday, prosecutor Lt. Scott McDonald claimed the tracking effort was to collect data such as IP addresses, which have no expectation of privacy, and was not meant to snoop on the content of the emails.</p><br/><div style="width:500px; word-wrap:break-word; font-size:80%;"><img src="https://a57.foxnews.com/static.foxnews.com/foxnews.com/content/uploads/2019/06/640/320/cmdrczaplak720.jpg?ve=1&tl=1" width=500px style="padding-bottom:0.5em;" /><br/>\n      Cmdr. Christopher Czaplak\n      (U.S. Navy)</div><br/><p>"We're talking about raw data," said McDonald, who argued that "even if there was some intrusion" in violation of attorney-client privilege, it didn't rise to the level necessary to dismiss the case.</p><p>But, Rugh chided Navy investigators who refused to testify Friday about who authorized the tracking scheme, saying the "lack of candor or cooperation in this process, I think, could be huge as a sign of culpability." The defense discovered the tracking code hidden in a suspicious logo of an American flag with a bald eagle perched on the scales of justice beneath Czaplak's signature.</p><p>Rugh indicated Friday he was misled about the tracking effort. He said investigators told him privately they planned to embed code in what he believed to be a court document to help them find the source of leaks but the judge said he didn't have the power to authorize such a tactic and wasn't told they planned to target emails sent to the defense lawyers or a journalist.</p><p>Gallagher is accused of stabbing to death a 15-year old ISIS fighter in Iraq in 2017, shooting two civilians in the same year and opening fire on crowds, all charges to which he has pleaded not guilty.</p><p>His platoon supervisor, Lt. Jacob Portier, has been fighting charges of conduct unbecoming an officer for allegedly conducting Gallagher's re-enlistment ceremony next to the militant's corpse.</p><p>The case has drawn the attention of President Trump, who reportedly has considered pardoning Gallagher along with other U.S. troops accused or convicted of war crimes.</p><p><i>Fox News' Vandana Rambaran and The Associated Press contributed to this report.</i></p>	https://www.foxnews.com/us/navy-seal-eddie-gallagher-prosecutor-removed-military-judge	changchaishi	2019-06-06 05:54:33.075711

27795c9a-ebad-4960-b47d-f00bfea0ddc8	Trump joins world leaders to commemorate 75th anniversary of D-Day	By MERIDITH MCGRAW	<p>President Donald Trump and first lady Melania Trump, on the third day of their U.K. trip, joined Queen Elizabeth II and more than 300 D-Day veterans in Portsmouth on Wednesday for a national ceremony of remembrance on the 75th anniversary of the allied military invasion remembered as a turning point of World War II.</p><br/><div style="width:500px; word-wrap:break-word; font-size:80%;"><img src="https://s.abcnews.com/images/Politics/trump-melania-gty-jpo-190605_hpEmbed_17x11_992.jpg" width=500px style="padding-bottom:0.5em;" /><br/>President Donald Trump and First Lady Melania Trump attend an event to commemorate the 75th anniversary of the D-Day landings, in Portsmouth, southern England, June 5, 2019. </div><br/><p>Portsmouth, a major port city in southern England, was the launching point for D-Day landings on June 6 and the home of Southwick House, headquarters for allied commander U.S. Gen. Dwight D. Eisenhower.</p><br/><div style="width:500px; word-wrap:break-word; font-size:80%;"><img src="https://s.abcnews.com/images/Politics/trump-queen-gty-jpo-190605_hpEmbed_17x11_992.jpg" width=500px style="padding-bottom:0.5em;" /><br/>Queen Elizabeth II and President, Donald Trump attend the D-day 75 Commemorations on June 05, 2019 in Portsmouth, England.</div><br/><p>President Trump, seated next to the queen in the royal box listened to tributes and performances commemorating the 1944 Normandy landings.</p><p>After reviewing honor guards from the Royal Navy, Army, Air Force and Welsh Guards, the president took the stage to read the prayer President Franklin D. Roosevelt delivered to the nation by radio on the evening of June 6, 1944, addressing the Normandy operation.</p><br/><div style="width:500px; word-wrap:break-word; font-size:80%;"><img src="https://s.abcnews.com/images/Politics/dda-gty-jpo-190605_hpEmbed_3x2_992.jpg" width=500px style="padding-bottom:0.5em;" /><br/>President Donald Trump gives a reading during the D-Day Commemorations on June 5, 2019 in Portsmouth, England.</div><br/><p>“Almighty God: Our sons, pride of our Nation, this day have set upon a mighty endeavour, a struggle to preserve our Republic, our religion, and our civilization, and to set free a suffering humanity," Trump read in an excerpt.</p><br/><div style="width:500px; word-wrap:break-word; font-size:80%;"><img src="https://s.abcnews.com/images/Politics/d-day-gty-jpo-190605_hpEmbed_3x2_992.jpg" width=500px style="padding-bottom:0.5em;" /><br/>D-Day veterans are presented on stage during an event to commemorate the 75th anniversary of the D-Day landings, in Portsmouth, southern England, June 5, 2019.</div><br/><p>Veterans of the 1944 invasion sat near the front for the ceremony with ribbons and medals on their chests. In addition to the queen, Trump was joined by Prince Charles, U.K. Prime Minister Theresa May, German Chancellor Angela Merkel, French President Emmanuel Macron and Canadian Prime Minister Justin Trudeau in the special tribute at Southsea Common.</p><br/><div style="width:500px; word-wrap:break-word; font-size:80%;"><img src="https://s.abcnews.com/images/Politics/dday-jpo-gty-jpo-190605_hpEmbed_13x11_992.jpg" width=500px style="padding-bottom:0.5em;" /><br/>President Donald Trump and Queen Elizabeth II join other dignitaries for the official family photograph during an event to commemorate the 75th anniversary of the D-Day landings, in Portsmouth, southern England, June 5, 2019.</div><br/><p>Trump, May, Macron and Trudeau read special tributes to their individual country's contributions, and the queen delivered an address before a Royal Navy frigate fires a naval salute and 25 historic and U.K. military aircraft fly over the proceedings.</p><p>Queen Elizabeth stated when she attended the 60th anniversary of D-Day, many believed it would be the last such commemoration. “But the wartime generation - my generation - is resilient, and I am delighted to be with you in Portsmouth today,” the 93-year-old queen said.</p><br/><div style="width:500px; word-wrap:break-word; font-size:80%;"><img src="https://s.abcnews.com/images/Politics/trump-melania-rt-jpo-190605_hpEmbed_3x2_992.jpg" width=500px style="padding-bottom:0.5em;" /><br/>President Donald Trump and First Lady Melania Trump meet veterans during the D-Day 75 National Commemorative event in Portsmouth, England, June 5, 2019. </div><br/><p>Following the ceremony, the president, first lady, the queen, Prince Charles and Macron met with a dozen D-Day veterans. Some 300 of them were headed to board the Royal British Legion's ship to depart for Normandy.</p><br/><div style="width:500px; word-wrap:break-word; font-size:80%;"><img src="https://s.abcnews.com/images/Politics/macron-d-day-gty-jpo-190605_hpEmbed_17x12_992.jpg" width=500px style="padding-bottom:0.5em;" /><br/>PHOTO:French President Emmanuel Macron shakes hands with a veteran as he returns to his seat during an event to commemorate the 75th anniversary of the D-Day landings, in Portsmouth, southern England, June 5, 2019.</div><br/><p>Trump and the queen bid each other farewell and taking a photo. “It was a great honor to be with you,” the president said to the queen calling her a "great woman."</p><p>On Thursday, the president will travel to Normandy to visit the Normandy American Cemetery in Colleville-sur-Mer, observe re-enactments of airborne landings and participate in a Commemoration of D-Day Program alongside veterans who stormed the beaches.</p><p>The two days of events are expected to be the last that many surviving World War II veterans are able to attend. From D-Day through Aug. 21 of that year, the Allies landed more than 2 million troops in northern France and suffered more than 226,000 casualties.</p><br/><div style="width:500px; word-wrap:break-word; font-size:80%;"><img src="https://s.abcnews.com/images/International/british-normandy-d-day-landing-2-ap-jc-190604_hpEmbed_18x13_992.jpg" width=500px style="padding-bottom:0.5em;" /><br/>Wounded British troops from the South Lancashire and Middlesex regiments are being helped ashore at Sword Beach, June 6, 1944, during the D-Day invasion of German occupied France during World War II.</div><br/><p>"More than one-and-a-half million American service members were stationed right here in England in advance of the landings that summer," Trump said of Portsmouth during a press conference with May on Tuesday. "The bonds of friendship forged here and sealed in blood on those hallowed beaches will endure forever."</p><br/><div style="width:500px; word-wrap:break-word; font-size:80%;"><img src="https://s.abcnews.com/images/Politics/trump-may-presser2-gty-ml-190604_hpMain_4x3_992.jpg" width=500px style="padding-bottom:0.5em;" /><br/>President Donald Trump and Britain's Prime Minister Theresa May give a joint press conference at the Foreign and Commonwealth office in London, June 4, 2019.</div><br/><p>May said the event aims to "reaffirm the enduring importance of the Western alliance and the shared values that underpin it."</p><p>After the Portsmouth celebration, the Trumps were headed to Shannon, Ireland, for a meeting with Irish Taoiseach Leo Varadkar before heading to Normandy.</p><p><em>\nABC News' Rachel Scott contributed to this report.</em></p>	https://abcnews.go.com/Politics/president-donald-trump-joins-world-leaders-pay-tribute/story?id=63482878&cid=clicksource_77_null_headlines_hed	changchaishi	2019-06-06 05:53:35.678443

--
-- Name: account account_email_key; Type: CONSTRAINT; Schema: public; Owner: news_manager
--

ALTER TABLE ONLY public.account
    ADD CONSTRAINT account_email_key UNIQUE (email);


--
-- Name: account account_pkey; Type: CONSTRAINT; Schema: public; Owner: news_manager
--

ALTER TABLE ONLY public.account
    ADD CONSTRAINT account_pkey PRIMARY KEY (username);


--
-- Name: article article_pkey; Type: CONSTRAINT; Schema: public; Owner: news_manager
--

ALTER TABLE ONLY public.article
    ADD CONSTRAINT article_pkey PRIMARY KEY (article_id);


--
-- Name: news news_pkey; Type: CONSTRAINT; Schema: public; Owner: news_manager
--

ALTER TABLE ONLY public.news
    ADD CONSTRAINT news_pkey PRIMARY KEY (id);


--
-- Name: products products_pkey; Type: CONSTRAINT; Schema: public; Owner: news_manager
--

ALTER TABLE ONLY public.products
    ADD CONSTRAINT products_pkey PRIMARY KEY (id);
